## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? -> `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? -> `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? -> `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? -> `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? -> `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search -> read -> references -> definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM SelectionDAG Assertion Failure Diagnosis

## Your Task

A production build system using LLVM is crashing with the error: 'Cannot expand this type; LLVM lacks the right hooks'. Trace this assertion to its source in `llvm/llvm-project`. Find: 1. The C++ source file in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/` that contains this error message or assertion. 2. The function in that file where the assertion fires (look for type legalization expansion logic). 3. The header file that defines the `EVT` (Extended Value Type) class and its `isSimple()` method (look in `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/`). 4. The file that defines the `LegalizeDAG` class which orchestrates type legalization and may call the expand function. Report the repo, file path, and function or class name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- `"Cannot expand node"` — in `ExpandNode()` at line 4698 of `LegalizeDAG.cpp`

**`ExpandNode(SDNode *Node)`** — `LegalizeDAG.cpp`, line 3218 (inside `SelectionDAGLegalize`)

Called by `LegalizeOp()` (line 972) when a node's operation must be expanded. If `ExpandNode` returns `false`, `LegalizeOp` falls back to `ConvertNodeToLibcall`. The type-specific expansion functions `ExpandIntegerResult` and `ExpandFloatResult` (in `DAGTypeLegalizer`) fire the equivalent fatal errors for type legalization.

It transforms\\\\n10: // an arbitrary well-formed SelectionDAG to only consist of legal types.  This\\\\n11: // is common code shared among the LegalizeTypes*.cpp files.\\\\n12: //\\\\n13: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\\\n14: \\\\n15: #include \\\\\\\"LegalizeTypes.h\\\\\\\"\\\\n16: #include \\\\\\\"llvm/ADT/SetVector.h\\\\\\\"\\\\n17: #include \\\\\\\"llvm/IR/DataLayout.h\\\\\\\"\\\\n18: #include \\\\\\\"llvm/Support/CommandLine.h\\\\\\\"\\\\n19: #include \\\\\\\"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\\\\\\\"\\\\n20: #include \\\\\\\"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\\\\\\\"\\\\n21: using namespace llvm;\\\\n22: \\\\n23: #define DEBUG_TYPE \\\\\\\"legalize-types\\\\\\\"\\\\n24: \\\\n25: static cl::opt\\\\u003cbool\\\\u003e\\\\n26: EnableExpensiveChecks(\\\\\\\"enable-legalize-types-checking\\\\\\\", cl::Hidden);\\\\n27: \\\\n28: /// Do extensive, expensive, basic correctness checking.\\\\n29: void DAGTypeLegalizer::PerformExpensiveChecks() {\\\\n30:   // If a node is not processed, then none of its values should be mapped by any\\\\n31:   // of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\\\\n32: \\\\n33:   // If a node is processed, then each value with an illegal type must be mapped\\\\n34:   // by exactly one of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\\\\n35:   // Values with a legal type may be mapped by ReplacedValues, but not by any of\\\\n36:   // the other maps.\\\\n37: \\\\n38:   // Note that these invariants may not hold momentarily when processing a node:\\\\n39:   // the node being processed may be put in a map before being marked Processed.\\\\n40: \\\\n41:   // Note that it is possible to have nodes marked NewNode in the DAG.  This can\\\\n42:   // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\\\\n43:   // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\\\\n44:   // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\\\\n45:   // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\\\\n46:   // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\\\\n47:   // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\\\\n48:   // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\\\\n49:   // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\\\\n50:   // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\\\\n51:   // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\\\\n52:   // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\\\\n53:   // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\\\\n54:   // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\\\\n55:   // to live on in the DAG.\\\\n56:   // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\\\\n57:   // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\\\\n58:   // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\\\\n59:   // not used by them.\\\\n60: \\\\n61:   // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\\\\n62:   // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\\\\n63: \\\\n64:   // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\\\\n65:   // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\\\\n66: \\\\n67:   // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\\\\n68:   // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).
